<div id="review_1421271660" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1421271660" />
    <a title="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads"><img alt="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566850655p2/16219087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1421271660?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads">Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1421271660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1299750687397230227">First of all: YAY I FINALLY FINISHED A BOOK FOR THE FIRST TIME IN LIKE OVER A WEEK WOOOO. Now on to the actual(ish) review! I AM SO MAD AT MYSELF FOR WAITING SO LONG TO READ THIS. I've had it on my shelf for years and finally decided to pick it up on a whim and WOW. I loved it SO MUCH. I want the next ones already bc I am dying to know how it ends!!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103248114" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103248114" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103248114?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141333663" href="/book/show/9533922-across-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=scifi-dystopian-apocalyptic">scifi-dystopian-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=love-story-romance">love-story-romance</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=not-afraid-of-sex-in-ya">not-afraid-of-sex-in-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=swapped-or-given-away">swapped-or-given-away</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103248114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13037631525955110782">4.5 stars. The spaceship <i>Goodspeed</i> is on its 300 years long journey to an inhabitable planet, Centauri-Earth. On board are about hundred specialists and their families (bio-engineers, tacticians, sociologists) stored as frozen human cargo in the deep and forgotten bowels of the huge vessel as well as two and a half thousand common inhabitants, who either research plants, weather and livestock for the future socialization or farm and produce goods for the small community. Since an obscure past ev</span>
  <span id="freeText13037631525955110782" style="display:none">4.5 stars. The spaceship <i>Goodspeed</i> is on its 300 years long journey to an inhabitable planet, Centauri-Earth. On board are about hundred specialists and their families (bio-engineers, tacticians, sociologists) stored as frozen human cargo in the deep and forgotten bowels of the huge vessel as well as two and a half thousand common inhabitants, who either research plants, weather and livestock for the future socialization or farm and produce goods for the small community. Since an obscure past event referred to as "The Plague" severed all connections to Sol-Earth and decimated the breathing population, the on-board democracy has been replaced by a the firm rule of a string of single and almighty rulers, who control access to the Earth's (tampered with) and the ship's (partly hazy) history, the use of cameras, the knowledge about what sleeps in the storage chambers, and who exchanged random reproduction for a system of one mating season per generation. The present ruler, Eldest, appears to be reluctant to share his vast knowledge with his still teen-aged successor, Elder, but emphasizes that the greatest dangers to a surviving society are differences between the members and lack of leadership. Slighted and unsatisfied Elder snoops around and discovers the already melting Amy, who is not only non-essential to the ship's mission (aka disposable if in the way), but also red-headed, pale and a powerful threat to Eldest's omnipotence. Elder's world view is shaken up: What else has been hidden from him and who is attempting to murder those who represent the pathway to a successful settlement?<br /><br />When I compare "Across the Universe" to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7059135.Inside_Out__Inside_Out___1_" title="Inside Out (Inside Out, #1) by Maria V. Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">Inside Out</a> by Maria V. Snyder, which also takes place in a small, confined and heavily controlled world/eco-system, I have to say I prefer "Inside Out". But, nonetheless, I loved "Across the Universe", too, and look forward to reading the sequel next year, because ...<br /><br />- It kept me glued to the pages to that extent that I was ripping my eyes open again and again last night while my husband already snored through his third dream or so<br />- I am a sucker for multi-point-of-view-stories, especially those switching between a boy and a girl<br />- I really love on-board-of-spaceship-novels that do not primarily deal with war (I also recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/234501.Startide_Rising__The_Uplift_Saga___2_" title="Startide Rising (The Uplift Saga, #2) by David Brin" rel="nofollow noopener">Startide Rising</a> and I greedily wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9035996.Molly_Fyde_and_the_Parsona_Rescue" title="Molly Fyde and the Parsona Rescue by Hugh Howey" rel="nofollow noopener">Molly Fyde and the Parsona Rescue</a> to be delivered to my postbox)<br />- I enjoyed that Beth Revis did not deliver a soppy romance in a thin and superficial space-travel wrapping, but a thrilling space mystery with fantastic world building and a pleasant sprinkling of boy-girl-attraction.<br />- The characters - even the side-crew - were well-defined, hard-angled and interesting<br />- Think-worthy questions about leadership, free will and the perfect socialization are touched on the way without offering simple answers.<br /><br />I recommend this piece of dystopian young adult fiction and say "Beth, bring on the sequel! You've earned all that praise."<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13037631525955110782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129830672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129830672" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320017147p2/4515165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129830672?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=premise-i-love">premise-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=falling-asleep">falling-asleep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=should-have-been-better">should-have-been-better</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129830672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12953689942748456641">I really, REALLY wanted to love Across the Universe. I've been eagerly anticipating this book for months. And then...I started reading. And it put me to sleep three nights in a row.<br/><br/>I hate that feeling when a book you've looked forward to for so long turns out to be...meh.<br/><br/>Part of my problem? I read Maria V. Snyder's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7059135.Inside_Out__Insider___1_' title='Inside Out (Insider, #1) by Maria V. Snyder' rel='nofollow noopener'>Inside Out</a> last week, and I couldn't help but make comparisons with Inside Out so fresh in my mind. Inside Out is so unique and compelling that Across the Universe felt flat, weary, a</span>
  <span id="freeText12953689942748456641" style="display:none">I really, REALLY wanted to love Across the Universe. I've been eagerly anticipating this book for months. And then...I started reading. And it put me to sleep three nights in a row.<br /><br />I hate that feeling when a book you've looked forward to for so long turns out to be...meh.<br /><br />Part of my problem? I read Maria V. Snyder's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7059135.Inside_Out__Insider___1_" title="Inside Out (Insider, #1) by Maria V. Snyder" rel="nofollow noopener">Inside Out</a> last week, and I couldn't help but make comparisons with Inside Out so fresh in my mind. Inside Out is so unique and compelling that Across the Universe felt flat, weary, and (frankly, in some parts) disturbing in comparison.<br /><br />(As an aside, I highly recommend Inside Out for sci-fi lite, dystopian fans. It's a little tedious in the beginning with all of the technical descriptions--props to Across the Universe for including the ship diagram--but Inside Out hits its stride and turns into a riveting tale of life contained inside a metal cube of secrets.)<br /><br />I admit--I had lofty expectations for Across the Universe, which affected my enjoyment. The novel has such a promising premise--I love the idea of blurring the genres into a this sci-fi mystery romance in a dystopian world--and I guess I was just expecting too much. The characters weren't unlikeable, but I didn't find myself really cheering for them, either. The best character in the novel went the way of Cogon from Inside Out, and I'm disappointed this character won't be back for the sequel.<br /><br />The worst part of Across the Universe is the overuse of "The Season" hammer. I get it--the Season is disturbing and creepy and unnatural--but I felt like Revis kept hitting me over the head with it again and again. I think a few mentions would have been okay since it is important to the plot, but I feel like I spent the entire middle of the book scrunching my nose and saying, "Eeeew, gross." I wanted to scrub my mind with some disinfectant afterward.<br /><br />Across the Universe was not a terrible read, but it just never felt completely engaging and compelling--I never had that crazy obsessed feeling you get when you're reading the most amazing book and just CANNOT. PUT. IT. DOWN.<br /><br />Across the Universe poses some intriguing questions regarding survival, leadership, free will, individual thought, and differences in society, and I hope these ideas will be explored in even greater depth in the sequel, as some of the answers at the end felt too simplistic. It was too black and white without enough exploration of the characters' motivations. The mystery is a little obvious and you'll figure it out way before Elder and Amy, but it did add another dimension to the novel. However, for me, Across the Universe did not live up to the hype.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12953689942748456641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_104517860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104517860" />
    <a title="Princess Bookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1218813-princess-bookie"><img alt="Princess Bookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243916881p2/1218813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104517860?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Princess Bookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Princess Bookie" href="/user/show/1218813-princess-bookie">Princess Bookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218813-princess-bookie?shelf=read2010">read2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104517860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4180251896650893517">My Thoughts: Wow, Wow, Wow! I tend to stay away from Sci-fi based novels but this one blew me away. As soon as I saw the summary I knew I wanted to read it, than the cover alone is worth buying it over. <br/><br/>We are introduced to Amy right away and her thoughts and feelings. She is getting ready to be frozen and even the very beginning of the book is very intense. The first few pages made my stomach hurt because I felt so sorry for her because the decision she had to make was huge. Than a few pages la</span>
  <span id="freeText4180251896650893517" style="display:none">My Thoughts: Wow, Wow, Wow! I tend to stay away from Sci-fi based novels but this one blew me away. As soon as I saw the summary I knew I wanted to read it, than the cover alone is worth buying it over. <br /><br />We are introduced to Amy right away and her thoughts and feelings. She is getting ready to be frozen and even the very beginning of the book is very intense. The first few pages made my stomach hurt because I felt so sorry for her because the decision she had to make was huge. Than a few pages later we meet Elder. He is the future leader of the ship; the Godspeed. He is being trained to take over the ship and lead his generation to their new home. <br /><br />Amy ends up getting woken up early and Elder does everything he can to try to make her more comfortable. He is very intrigued by this new girl. She is so different from everyone on the ship, her personality, her hair color, her looks, just everything. He finds her fascinating. Of course the leader of the ship right now, Elder does not like her at all. He finds her to be a nuisance and wants her gone. <br /><br />Their are so many secrets, lies, mysteries on the ship that there is never a dull moment and we are constantly learning new things. Amy's parents are still frozen and she fears they will be woken up just like she was, which she knows now was not an accident because a few others have been unfrozen left to die. And than there is The Season. It's basically where everyone starts mating to reproduce to keep the ships population going on. I hated it from the get go! Love needs to be natural, not predestined. I understand they need to keep humans on the ship but I wanted people to fall in love! <br /><br />I also loved all the characters in Across The Universe. There were a lot of side characters to keep the story going. I liked getting to know them all.<br /><br />No spoilers in this review because I don't want to spoil it for anyone so just read the book to find out what happens! What happens to Amy? Does she ever make it off the ship? Does Elder become leader? When does the ship land? <br /><br />Overall: I really loved this one. I'm usually not a big fan of sci-fi type books. I tend to stick with paranormal or contemp romance YA but this one had just striked my fancy. It was a wonderful book! Its a pretty thick book but I finished it within a day. Once I started, I didn't want to stop. I just had to know what was going to happen!!! It was also told in separate points of view so we got to experience things both with Amy and Elder!Loved that!<br /><br />Cover: The cover is beautiful. Its striking with just the right amount of colors. Very unique and pretty. <br /><br />What I'd Give It: 5/5 Cupcakes<br /><br />Taken from Princess Bookie<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.princessbookie.com">www.princessbookie.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4180251896650893517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_148213924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148213924" />
    <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship"><img alt="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297107033p2/2109885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/148213924?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship">Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141333663" href="/book/show/9533922-across-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=series-abandoned">series-abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=m-read">m-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=dystopian-or-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-or-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148213924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3631785665568838706"><u>
  <b>Lessons learned</b>
</u>:<br/>Never trust history.<br/>Never trust doctors.<br/>Never trust scientists.<br/>Never trust technology.<br/>Never trust blanket medication.<br/><br/>Overall my experience with this book was like meeting and falling in love, being excited and happy, then slowly finding out that he's not perfect. He drinks out of the milk carton, he ignores you in favour of sports events and when you finally get his clothes off he's as smooth as a Ken doll but insists he can still have children. Then finding out he's right he</span>
  <span id="freeText3631785665568838706" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>Lessons learned</b>
</u>:<br />Never trust history.<br />Never trust doctors.<br />Never trust scientists.<br />Never trust technology.<br />Never trust blanket medication.<br /><br />Overall my experience with this book was like meeting and falling in love, being excited and happy, then slowly finding out that he's not perfect. He drinks out of the milk carton, he ignores you in favour of sports events and when you finally get his clothes off he's as smooth as a Ken doll but insists he can still have children. Then finding out he's right he can make babies, just not the same enjoyable way everyone else does, which is confusing and unsatisfying. <br /><br /><b>If you're going to write science fiction, could you at least research the science? Please, please get your facts right, if you don't then you must sell this as fantasy not SF.</b><br /><br />I assumed, not even 50% in, that I was reading unscientific science fiction i.e. fantasy. As far as I was concerned the author had made little attempt to research certain aspects of her story so why was I wasting my time reading it? I was THIS close to giving up. It was almost as disastrous as my experience with the scientifically unsound <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7747374.I_am_Number_Four__Lorien_Legacies___1_" title="I am Number Four (Lorien Legacies, #1) by Pittacus Lore" rel="nofollow noopener">I am Number Four</a>. Little did I know that if I had given up, I would've missed out on the <b>explanations which magically fixed many of the obstacles that I'd previously believed were unquestionably insurmountable because science told me so</b>, and therefore the cure-all bandage Revis slaps on the problems didn't sit right with me. They were hard to accept in the face of catastrophically fatal situations. There is a lesson in this: <b>if it reads like unintelligent drivel some readers may give up on your work before you make the big reveal that attempts to explain the drivel</b>.<br /><br />Amy's character is well-drawn and <b>her memories and emotions are brilliantly portrayed</b>. I had some difficulty with Elder's character but his personality was a result of Eldest's manipulation and his awakening is caused by Amy's inquisitiveness and tenaciousness. I was glad he was finally able to see the truth of things. <br /><br /><b>Harley and his girlfriend were an excellent examples of people not being able to cope under the pressure of living on the claustrophobic ship surrounded by fakery</b> (there is no substitute for the real thing) because despite his mood swings and obsession problem they were both perfectly sane, despite being labelled crazy. <br /><br />It was completely understandable the almost absurd lengths Eldest went to to impose and maintain the many methods of manipulation in order for everyone to survive. <b>Survival was imperative. Quality of life means nothing in the face of that. Or does it?</b> And that's what this questions.<br /><br /><b>This society may not believe in any religion as we know it but they do have religion: hope.</b> Hope is their "opium of the masses" (a Marxist philosophy on the merits of religion) which is a method of control. By giving the people hope that their sacrifices will ensure that their children will be the ones to one day see real sky above their heads and feel earth beneath their feet, keeps them going, keeps them working, living, breathing. Without hope what is there?<br /><br /><b>There are moments, scenes, words of wisdom -that are pure genius and others where I felt baffled, confused and angry when I think I'm reading utter crap.</b> Ideas have been stolen from movies like <i>Serenity</i> (Phydus is Pax) and the less popular <i>Demolition Man</i> (being conscious in cryo) which makes me wonder how much of this book is original. There is no romance despite the cover (Elder is interested in Amy but not vice versa), and we know who the killer is before the search even begins. Bevis gets the human element right but the science and mystery completely wrong. It's a real mixed bag and it's difficult for me to determine my position on this book, positive or negative. A five star beginning graduating to a one star ending?<br /><br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Timeline of my reading experience (i.e. like status updates)</b>
</u><br /><br />~ Hooked by page 10 and in love by page 11. I am in love. And I am not a cheap date. But why don't they knock 'em out before starting the freezing process? Much less painful and traumatising. This is not something I'd want to go through.<br /><br />~ I'd want my extra year on Earth back too, honey, but life ain't fair. Best you learn that now. You chose this, I wouldn't have. Deal with it. <br /><br />~ Reminded of the movie <i>Demolition Man</i> (and a little of <i>The Matrix</i>) here. They're both conscious during their cryo state. How does she not go crazy?<br /><br />~ Jarred by the second POV, Amy is more than enough for me. I like her. I like her a lot. I want her to live. So <b>why does she never get her blood back during reanimation?</b> She's literally blue-blooded now. She IS a freak!<br /><br />~ Frexing? Brilly? Chutz? Are there <b>only three new words in 250 years</b>? That's unrealistic. Language in the 1760s was different to today. The author probably should've left these out instead of calling attention to it. <br /><br />~ Why do they <b>repeatedly</b> say the generational Elder between Elder Jnr and Eldest is dead? He's obviously not. And he's probably the killer.<br /><br />~ I've noticed a small thing and it's got me thinking about the science in this science fiction. The plague killed off many, decreasing the on-board free-range population to the 700s -this is where I couldn't help but question the MVP (<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minimum_viable_population" rel="nofollow noopener">minimum viable population</a>). Taking into consideration the 100 frozen battery humans, I do a quick Google search and the <a href="http://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0006320707002534" rel="nofollow noopener">result</a> is not good. <b>Extinction, a foregone conclusion.</b> In theory you need more than 3,000 individuals for a species to survive. So why read the rest? Because I'm in lurve and this will be amazing. Nothing will spoil this. Nothing! <br /><br />~ I like fresh air. <i>*opens window*</i><br /><br />~ That old man. He's going to heaven sooner than he thinks, isn't he? I just know it. Well, that solves the pensions crisis.<br /><br />~ Um, <b>if incest is an issue with such a small population, why is everyone indiscriminately bonking?</b> Be ready for the possibility of birth defects in the next generation. Also, why are those in their twenties the only ones to go through their Season? Shouldn't everyone older as well as the supposed crazies plus Amy, Elder, Eldest, Doc etc. be bonking their brains out? <br /><br />~ <b>Halfway in and we've turned away from a possible romance as advertised on the cover and we're ignoring Elder's boner around Amy's red hair.</b> No, now we're solving a murder. Whaaaaat? Elder is all talk. I thought he was going to use that boner to show Eldest who's boss. Er, that didn't come out right. I meant, he was going defy Eldest by making love to that (girl with the) beautiful red hair and then usurp/depose Eldest. Oh, and quietly but quickly solve the whodunnit. Elder is a disappointing hero.<br /><br />~ I liked my priorities. Why aren't my priorities Amy's priorities. Look, love, you've been frozen for centuries, without boys, there's a cute muscley one in front of you, you have hormones, go get 'im!<br /><br />~ She refuses to listen. <b>We must find clues to who likes to unplug frozen people. Yawn. We, the reader, all ready know who it is, why bother?</b> There is no mystery to solve for us but we have to watch and wait for the characters slowly put things together. Tedious.<br /><br />~ Let's get rid of the Hitler-worshipping Nazi instead, shall we? Anything but crime-solving. Anything! A threesome with Harley? It promises to be colourful and sticky. Well, more sticky. No? <i>*whines*</i><br /><br />~ <b>
  <i>CSI:Godspeed</i>
</b> is on the job!<br /><br />~ Those fingerprints tell me the Eldest/Elders are <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[clones. I wonder how this came to be and how they're brought to term if they have no mothers. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />~ Soon there'll be no frozens left to help colonise Centauri. <b>This ship is doomed.</b><br /><br />~ Dragggggging. Not much happening.<br /><br /><i>*flips to the back*</i><br /><br />Oh, a map. I didn't know there was one. <br /><br /><i>*reads the last 40 pages* </i><br /><br /><b>That's it?! That's how it ends?!</b> But...but that was too easy. No mystery to it, and I was right all along. No surprises, no realisation that they're on a failed mission.<br /><br />Amy should've stayed on Earth, run the New York marathon and married Jason. That was obviously her heart's desire. Her father knew that, it's a shame she didn't. Mind you, it wasn't fair of him to give her the choice at the last minute. She made a decision under pressure and panic had her following her parents. <br /><br /><i>*back to reading, well, skimming...*</i><br /><br />~ Attempted rape. I thought Elder said there was no crime now. Hormones are no excuse.<br /><br /><blockquote>'And I know without being told that she killed herself. And I totally understand why.' Me too. I don't envy their lives. </blockquote><br /><br />~ <b>Incest and MVP problem solved but not in a way I completely accept</b> although I'm feeling very wary of medicine and scientists right now.<br /><br />~ <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They’ve been travelling for more than 300 years. The Plague –suicide, murder, riots, chaos. A never-ending journey. 250 years behind schedule. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <b>I was right, they are doomed!</b><br /><blockquote>”People will survive anything for their children.”</blockquote><br />p336 ~ The seasons, the generations and other methods of manipulation all make more sense now. <br /><br /><blockquote>“We’re just pawns. A means to an end. Toys you manufacture to keep playing your game.”</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The 3 main causes of discord:</u>
</b><br />1) Difference<br />2) Lack of leadership<br />3) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>
    <i>Individual thought</i>
  </b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />~ <b>SERENITY!</b> – A big whopping dose of the movie, <i>Serenity</i>. Pax = Phydus. No reavers but the other effect of the Pax in varying doses is exactly the same as Phydus. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Small doses = calm, large does = death) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />~ Recycling. They recycle EVERYTHING. People are treated like things. <i>*gulp*</i><br /><blockquote>‘[...] I realize the simple truth is that power isn’t control at all-power is strength, and giving that strength to others. A leader isn’t someone who forces others to make him stronger; a leader is someone willing to give his strength to stand on their own.' p344.</blockquote><br />I've read the end so...THE END.<br /><br /><br />*******I apologise for the extra long review but it was the only way to illustrate my frustrations.*******</span>
  <a data-text-id="3631785665568838706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_135418731" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135418731" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135418731?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101486085" href="/book/show/9996290-across-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=beloved">beloved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=sweet-romance">sweet-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135418731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18406512929395374638"><i>"A love out of time. A spaceship built of secrets and murder."</i><br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/beth-revis/across-the-universe-review.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342637i/698368.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>So.. <br/><br/># First - the cover is absolutely gorgeous (at least I love it) and this is what made me want to read this book.. And so the myth saying that a book with a great cover is always horrible is busted (just) for the moment ;))<br/><br/># Second, the cover and the beginning of the quote from above are just a bit wrong - this is not really a love story (not so far), we have some romance in it but it is a small part of this book compared to e</span>
  <span id="freeText18406512929395374638" style="display:none"><i>"A love out of time. A spaceship built of secrets and murder."</i><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/beth-revis/across-the-universe-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342637i/698368.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So.. <br><br># First - the cover is absolutely gorgeous (at least I love it) and this is what made me want to read this book.. And so the myth saying that a book with a great cover is always horrible is busted (just) for the moment ;))<br><br># Second, the cover and the beginning of the quote from above are just a bit wrong - this is not really a love story (not so far), we have some romance in it but it is a small part of this book compared to everything else.<br><br># Third - about the book... It's really hard to talk about it not wanting to spoil it for you.<br>It's strange but what I liked the most was the description.. not the description of the ship itself, but the descriptions of the dreams Amy had, of her feelings, of Elder's feelings for the strange girl with white skin and red hair. The description of this new society so strange and different, with those people that are more like aliens than humans. It's a great book, written in a wonderful way, and I just love every page of it.<br><br>We have this girl <b>Amy</b>, who loves Earth, and life on Earth, and more than that she loves her parents (mostly her dad) and wants to go with them when they decide to enroll for this adventure of finding a new planet to live on. We find out some things about her life on Earth, about her deceptions, and we find out more about what she misses from home, about her dreams and fears, about the way she sees the world. She tries to give us the definition of "normal".. but what normal really is?<br><br>Than we have <b>Elder</b> who doesn't find his place in a tiny world made of iron (the only world he knows) and who dreams about a new world infinite and not perfect and not symmetrical, and not hand-made. He is the next to rule over the people on this ship, but finding about the secrets this ship is keeping is not an easy task to do, and knowing is sometimes not better that not knowing at all.<br>I don't like when the main characters have such big responsibilities on their shoulders because they have to 'split' between love and duty and the development of those 2 sides of their personality is never enough to make that character stand out. Elder was a teenager and it was enough to see a girl he loved (a girl that was kind of forbidden) to forget about the fact that he was supposed to train to be a leader - his only purpose in life.<br><br>There story reminded me about 'The Hunger Games' just because Elder is the one that cares the most. At the end I can't tell if Amy liked him or not that much because her feeling are not that easy to figure out. Elder on the other way made us understand from the first moment he sees her that he is amazed by her beauty and he would want to keep her forever by his side, to love her all his life. For him is like love at first sight (or what love at first sight might mean in a such strange world that Godspeed is). We see him protecting her and her dreams, struggling between his duties and his feelings, and the more we know him the less we expect him to surprise us in any way, but he does.. <br><br><a href="http://grecian888.deviantart.com/art/Across-the-Universe-208632040" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342637i/698369._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Another important character is <b>Eldest</b>. You may see him as the "bad guy" in this story (everyone thinks that he is the Evil in person), the one that keeps so many secrets, the one that makes so many horrible things... and he might be.... but I don't really see him that way, I think that given the situation he made the best he could on those critical moments (and <i> I don't agree with him </i>, is not that, I just understand why he did all those things). Maybe there would have been other ways to keep the ship running (some more ethical ways), but desperate moments need desperate measures and the most he could do was keeping his people alive. I don't agree with the situation on the ship (God help us all to be in such an environment) but I can see how he didn't know better, how they were on their own, with no one to help them or give them an advice, with no one to tell if they are right or wrong, a tiny world in such a huge universe, all on their own. He was wrong about so many things but he didn't do all those things because he had a dark soul.. that's the most I can tell about him.<br>.... And we will see in the next installment if he was right or not, if there are better ways to run this ship, to be a better leader over those desperate people, if the truth is better than the lies, if the hope is not the one that keeps us moving.. and now I think that I just said too much. <br><br>About the <b>killer</b> - well I knew who the killer was from almost the beginning. I was a bit annoyed to see how no one noticed anything wrong about the killers attitude and all, and I was a bit more surprised about the revelation itself, about all that we found at the end of the book. I was like "OMG!.... no way" about so many things and my only regret is that the ending was so, so, soooo rushed.<br>This was the best part of the book from my point of view, when all the pieces of the puzzle fitted together for the first time, and there were things that I knew about, but some that I didn't see coming... And now I need to read this book again at least partially (to figure out why didn't I see it all coming)... But everything was so damn rushed and I couldn't keep up with all of it because even in one paragraph there was a lot to tell.. I don't know, it just gave me the impression that the author really needed to finish the book but wanted to tell us the full story in those few pages and it's a shame because in a way this is the part I liked the most. <br><br>And the last scene from the book is so strange, like the quiet before the storm, it scares me more than all those creepy scenes from the book. I'm not saying more, but I guess that in next book we will find out more.<br><br>Also, there are still questions that need to be answered - for example I want to know what did Eldest tell Harley near the end. This might be something unimportant for most of you, but that was why he made the decision he made and I would've liked to know him better, because he was one of my favorite character. And there are things that remained in the air (like some scene that leaves some marks on Amy's skin.. I don't want to spoil it for you and I won't insist about it, but still the scene was not resolved at all.)<br><br><br><b>Favorite quotes:</b><br><br><i>"I am as silent as death. <br>Do this: Go to your bedroom. Your nice, safe, warm bedroom that is not a glass coffin behind a morgue door. Lie down on your bed not made of ice. Stick your fingers in your ears. Do you hear that? The pulse of life from your heart, the slow in-and-out from your lungs? Even when you are silent, even when you block out all noise, your body is still a cacophony of life. Mine is not. It is the silence that drives me mad. The silence that drives the nightmares to me.<br>Because what if I am dead?" </i> ~ Amy<br><br><i>"I never thought about how important the sky was until I didn't have one."</i> ~ Amy<br><br><i>"I want to take her into my arms and hold her tight. But at the same time, I know that is the exact opposite of what she wants. She wants to be free, and all I want is to hold her tight against me."</i> ~ Elder<br><br><i>"When I look at the fields, all I can see is how fake they are, how poor an imitation they are of the pictures of Sol-Earth fields. [...] <br>And that's why I'll never be as good an Eldest as he is. <br>Because I like a little chaos."</i> ~ Elder<br><br><br>Now, some <b>notes</b>:<br><br>1. There are some scenes that are not described in detail, but they are definitely more than what YA should be about. I didn't enjoyed some of them but I guess there were important for us to see how twisted that 'world' was.<br><br>2. Also, I don't know what's the thing with the curse words in this book. If you feel like swearing just do it all the way.. if not, just keep it for yourself. Don't try to hide the sun behind your finger. My first words in English were "yes" ,"no" ,"fuck".. I think I can deal with reading that word just fine (thank you very much for your concern) and it's more annoying to read a " frexing " derivative of it.<br><br>3. I just don't know why people keep comparing this book with "The Host" because they are nothing alike (and I love them both).. except for the fact that the action takes place in the future, and the main interest in the story is the humanity, Earth, the beauty of life, love, etc.. Well, except for these 2 things, there is nothing that could possibly link these 2 books together.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/beth-revis/across-the-universe-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" width="361" height="116" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/beth-revis/across-the-universe-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

<div id="review_132652406" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132652406" />
    <a title="Nomes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes"><img alt="Nomes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499148999p2/3842653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132652406?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nomes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nomes" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes">Nomes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=alternating-m-f-pov">alternating-m-f-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=faves-of-2010">faves-of-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132652406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13214454832311409349">I'm just going to come right out and say it: This book was BRILLIANT and I absolutely LOVED every moment of it. I devoured it all through the night and have been thinking about it ever since (3 weeks ago).<br/><br/>Where to begin with my (rave-on) review?<br/><br/>It's epic, dystopian, has an impossible romance, mystery, creativity and lots of heart and soul. <br/><br/>The prose: Gorgeous and evocative. For a sci-fi it was so not complicated to follow - it flowed seamlessly. <br/><br/>The whole concept: Mate, it's so well explored. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText13214454832311409349" style="display:none">I'm just going to come right out and say it: This book was BRILLIANT and I absolutely LOVED every moment of it. I devoured it all through the night and have been thinking about it ever since (3 weeks ago).<br><br>Where to begin with my (rave-on) review?<br><br>It's epic, dystopian, has an impossible romance, mystery, creativity and lots of heart and soul. <br><br>The prose: Gorgeous and evocative. For a sci-fi it was so not complicated to follow - it flowed seamlessly. <br><br>The whole concept: Mate, it's so well explored. The world building felt flawless. It's in depth but so accessible. I can only imagine the immense thought and creativity involved in producing such a book. Exceptional stuff. It was so easy to imagine myself on board the Godspeed - a beautifully painted world. I loved being a part of it.<br><br>The characters: Loved them. Particularly Amy - I really felt for her, nothing was easy for her - (Revis does not suffer from the whole being kind to your characters syndrome :). There's some genuine moments where I was so moved with compassion and emotion. Also, the villains - ahh, complex with shades of good and bad, making the moral ambiguity so conflicting to read. Really well drawn.<br><br>The plotting: WOW. There's a lot to admire. As in, HOLY COW, it's just brilliantly plotted.<br><br>Twists and turns and mysteries and conspiracies. The stakes are continually raised and then something happens that you don't see coming and they are raised again. I thought I had things figured out but then Revis would throw a new spanner in the works and I'd be all whirling about again. Which is why I read it all through the night... unputdownable kinda stuff. Plus, she juggled all the world building, flashbacks, outer space, mystery, history and multi-POV. <br><br>Recommended: Absolutely one of my favourite reads this year. I am completely in awe of it. This is a book to suck in non-readers, males, fans of any genre. It's one my dad would enjoy as well as my teen niece. Even more - I recommend SNATCHING it up as a high school text. The themes in this book would be brilliantly explored in class discussion. A first class book from a talented new author. Just wow.<br><br>*note: there are some mature themes regarding, ahh, human mating :) <br><br><br>Here's my casting call :) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341897i/697870.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Karen Gillan as Amy (just imagine her a tad younger. PERFECT :)<br></span>

<div id="review_349441207" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349441207" />
    <a title="Denisse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse"><img alt="Denisse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606102662p2/8759700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349441207?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denisse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denisse" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse">Denisse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA Sci-Fi fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Denisse by: </span>
      What else? THE COVER. 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8759700-denisse?shelf=crushes">crushes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349441207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7579678640440693324"><b>With a fluent pace and fresh sci-fi/mystery elements, <i>Across the Universe</i> offers a light read mixed with some glimpses of serious topics.</b> The entire dynamic of the spaceship and how it is controlled was very well developed, and while it does takes some time to start the actual plot, the first pages are very interesting and well written. <b>Beth Revis has some of the best sci-fi ideas I have read about</b>, and even when I’d want her to do an adult book, her young adult light development is always refre</span>
  <span id="freeText7579678640440693324" style="display:none"><b>With a fluent pace and fresh sci-fi/mystery elements, <i>Across the Universe</i> offers a light read mixed with some glimpses of serious topics.</b> The entire dynamic of the spaceship and how it is controlled was very well developed, and while it does takes some time to start the actual plot, the first pages are very interesting and well written. <b>Beth Revis has some of the best sci-fi ideas I have read about</b>, and even when I’d want her to do an adult book, her young adult light development is always refreshing and smart without being over plotted or over explained. <br /><br />My <b>YA-2015-SEASON</b> continues...this is #4<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I never thought about how important the sky was until I didn't have one.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><b>Me encanta Beth Revis.</b> Siempre se me hace súper relajado y divertido leerla. Hay algo en sus libros e historias cortas que simplemente me fascina. Trae ideas muy frescas y las desarrolla bien a mi parecer. <br /><br />Esta trilogía en particular arranca con mucha fuerza. A pesar de que nuestros protagonistas Elder y Amy son jóvenes, la trama no esta cargada de romance, hay una o dos escenas por ahí pero nada <i>all-over-your-face</i>. Y esto hace que el misterio y lo sci-fi de la historia tome un protagónico que se disfruta mucho. <br /><br /><b>Lo mejor de Revis es que no explica lo inexplicable.</b> Sabe que hay cosas que no puede explicar con ciencia así que las deja como solo <i>ideas sueltas sci-fi</i> que ayudan a su trama. Mientras que otras si tienen explicación y las expone de forma rápida y concisa. <br /><br /><b>Si lo estuviera leyendo por primera vez ahora en pleno 2015, habría visto venir ciertos giros, pero la mayoría están bien escondidos en la trama.</b> Aunque, como es en realidad relectura de mi parte, pude apreciar ciertas pistas que iba dejando la autora que obviamente no vi la primera vez que lo leí. Y aunque sabia lo que iba a pasar, disfrute mucho la lectura. <br /><br />Aclarando que todo esta a un nivel YA, por lo tanto aunque se toquen temas como la tiranía, el control biológico o incluso algo sobre sexualidad bastante fuerte, no se siente demasiado oscuro o denso. Mucho de eso gracias a la escritura de Revis, bastante ligera. <b>Y eso es un gran acierto, el saber tocar temas delicados de forma juvenil.</b> No cualquiera lo puede hacer. <br /><br />Los personajes, sobretodo los 2 principales, me encantan. Tienen ese ímpetu rebelde típico de un adolescente pero con los atisbos de pensamientos maduros que de repente tiene uno a esa edad. Me encanta. Sus diferencias y las conversaciones que encabezan me encantan. <br /><br />Al final, <i>Across the Universe</i> queda como una lectura fácil, pero en la cual puedes encontrar intensidad y madurez dentro de ciertas subtramas si te das tiempo a leer detenidamente. <b>Recomendado si te gusta la ciencia ficción dentro del genero juvenil y estas en busca de algo amigable pero interesante. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7579678640440693324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118804932" />
    <a title="Nic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2813423-nic"><img alt="Nic" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118804932?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nic" href="/user/show/2813423-nic">Nic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=cover-crazy">cover-crazy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118804932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2995613140144958762">Favourite quote:- <i>“It is like a piece of my soul had been lost, empty, and it is now filled with the light of a million stars.”</i><br/><br/>Wow! What an amazing debut. Across the Universe is a book that you will get lost in and completely forget about the rest of the world. Utterly captivating.<br/><br/>It is unique with it’s mix of part space travel, part thriller and part romance. If you are worried that it sounds too sci-fi with all that space travel talk, it is not at all. It will definitely appeal to fans of para</span>
  <span id="freeText2995613140144958762" style="display:none">Favourite quote:- <i>“It is like a piece of my soul had been lost, empty, and it is now filled with the light of a million stars.”</i><br /><br />Wow! What an amazing debut. Across the Universe is a book that you will get lost in and completely forget about the rest of the world. Utterly captivating.<br /><br />It is unique with it’s mix of part space travel, part thriller and part romance. If you are worried that it sounds too sci-fi with all that space travel talk, it is not at all. It will definitely appeal to fans of paranormal, fantasy and even contemporary fiction. <br /><br />Revis is a clever writer with her engrossing and well thought out plot. There were so many layers to it. In the last 100 pages Revis really pulled out the surprises, leaving my mouth hanging open. And I can tell you now if somebody came up to me and asked if I would liked to get frozen and travel in space, even it included the gorgeous Elder (who I will get to in a minute), I would tell them NO and then run and hide. It would be scary to be stuck on that ship with all it is secrets. <br /><br />I know some of you are wondering about the ending, if it is a cliffhanger. Well let just say part of the story wraps up nicely and well the other part leaves you wanting more. Satisfying for now.<br /><br />Now on to the characters. This story is told from both Amy’s and Elder’s point of views and their worlds couldn’t be more different. Amy is probably my standout character. She is the kind of gal that asks questions and is determined to get to the truth and no matter what never gave up. Elder is a sweetheart and gorgeous who also shows a lot of strength when his whole world was coming crashing down on him. <br /><br />And the romance is beautiful with lines like this:<br /><br /><i>“I want to take her into my arms and hold her tight. But at the same time, I know that is the exact opposite of what she wants. She wants to be free and all I want to do is hold her tight against me.”</i><br /><br />Overall, I loved it. A must read for 2011!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2995613140144958762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=forclosettwilightfans">forclosettwilightfans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=ya-dystopia">ya-dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1263186151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16031415123184729576">This is a book that reminds me why you should NEVER trust goodreads ratings. By looking at the rating I really had low expectations about this book and guess what? I loved it! <br/><br/>For starters, this book wasn't like other sci-fi dystopians that are always so similar: Special girl who ends up being the key to everything, and forced romance. Nope this one was more sci-fi than dystopia.<br/><br/>Another thing I liked was the romance. It was just right amount, not too much to make the reading tacky and enough to </span>
  <span id="freeText16031415123184729576" style="display:none">This is a book that reminds me why you should NEVER trust goodreads ratings. By looking at the rating I really had low expectations about this book and guess what? I loved it! <br /><br />For starters, this book wasn't like other sci-fi dystopians that are always so similar: Special girl who ends up being the key to everything, and forced romance. Nope this one was more sci-fi than dystopia.<br /><br />Another thing I liked was the romance. It was just right amount, not too much to make the reading tacky and enough to keep me wondering and turning the pages at top speed.<br /><br />Worldbuilding was great, which is something that is not always common in YA dystopia. And the twist at the end, was a great addition to an already well constructed plot! It left me wanting more.<br /><br />I don't think this book is perfect by any means and I won't add it to my favorites, but as far as YA dystopia it deserves more love. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16031415123184729576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_646359252" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646359252" />
    <a title="Maddie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18523225-maddie"><img alt="Maddie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531656548p2/18523225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646359252?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie" href="/user/show/18523225-maddie">Maddie</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/15761655-across-the-universe">review of another edition</a>

The plot came to such a neat conclusion, and the relationship between Amy and Elder wasn't too over the top. Great plot twists, and an interesting environment...although I had a few questions about the logistics and motives, I was a good start to the series! (And not unlike an episode of Doctor Who.)</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_187481868" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187481868" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187481868?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=signed-by-author">signed-by-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187481868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16830249375582077601">Amy Martin is put into cryogenic freeze with her parents, to travel to a far distant world called Centauri-Earth, which the ship, <i>Godspeed</i> will reach in 300 years. But she is awakened suddenly and nearly dies in the process. Who woke her from her sleep and who is killing the others cryogenically frozen?<br/><br/>I love science fiction. I love Star Wars, Battlestar Galactica...even hard scifi, like Arthur C. Clarke. And when I started this book, I adored it! There is just far too little scifi out there in </span>
  <span id="freeText16830249375582077601" style="display:none">Amy Martin is put into cryogenic freeze with her parents, to travel to a far distant world called Centauri-Earth, which the ship, <i>Godspeed</i> will reach in 300 years. But she is awakened suddenly and nearly dies in the process. Who woke her from her sleep and who is killing the others cryogenically frozen?<br /><br />I love science fiction. I love Star Wars, Battlestar Galactica...even hard scifi, like Arthur C. Clarke. And when I started this book, I adored it! There is just far too little scifi out there in the young adult market right now. To me, this is a breath of fresh air.<br /><br />But alas, I can't just sing praises of this book and move on. While I did greatly enjoy this book, much like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183951783" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a>, a lot of the problems in this book are the result of technology/world building.<br /><br />REASONS WHY THIS WAS ENJOYABLE<br /><br />+ Amy. I liked how she sacrificed a lot to be with her parents (her boyfriend, dreams of running in a marathon, etc.). I liked how she didn't fall into insta-love with Elder or any of the other males on the ship. I also liked how she drove the investigation into the mysteries of the ship--the culture and the people being removed from cryofreeze. Even at the end, she plays an important role in the "Final Showndown".<br /><br />+ Elder. I liked how he was drawn to Amy because of her hair and how he was constantly thinking about "getting physical" with her. I felt that it was pretty realistic for a guy, without getting creepy or going too far. I liked how he was questioning his role as a leader before meeting Amy.<br /><br />+ No romance. As I said above, Amy and Elder don't immediately see each other and get all googly-eyed. In fact, there are times where Amy hates Elder. Even at the end, there is a hint of perhaps romance, but no kisses, no swooning.<br /><br />+ The Mystery. A lot of times, if people are thinking scifi, they may not think "mystery". Much like fantasy gets connected with elves and romance with heaving bosoms, scifi gets coupled with laser guns and aliens. This book really takes a different route, one that I really enjoyed following along. I loved trying to figure out the whodunnit (though sadly, I kinda guessed it very early on in the book).<br /><br />+ Thoughtful Questions. Is it right to rule people with an iron fist? What if the truth could be harmful? How much truth should you reveal? If you like books with thoughtful questions that don't get nicely wrapped up in ribbons and bows at the end, this is your book.<br /><br />+ The Ship. The idea of cryogenically freezing some people and leaving others to run the ship while en route was great. I loved how the ship society greatly changed (how Amy had some trouble understanding what they were saying because of the dialect) and evolved as the ship traveled through space (but...).<br /><br />REASONS WHY I WENT "HUH?!"<br /><br />+ Padding. This book could EASILY have had 100+ pages cropped from the middle. There was WAY too much time spent on the Season, the near-rape experience was 100% unnecessary (the results from this encounter were already FIRMLY hammered into the audience's head, and Amy is never nearly as traumatized by this event as she should be), Amy and Elder bring up questions, then proceed to wander around and do nothing. It's a shame, because when they FINALLY started to ask questions and WAIT for the answers, the book was completely gripping.<br /><br />+ Logistics. Having children only once per generation isn't going to repair the population crisis. In fact, it's likely to make it worse. Why bother with a Season in the first place when you could have all your women go to the doctor and be artificially inseminiated? That way you could control when the children were born and avoid incest in one shot. Engines do NOT work the same way in space (vacuum) as on Earth. They would NOT need to be kept running 24/7 to keep the ship moving, so this bullcrap about the ship's engines running at 40% maximum speed is WRONG. Newton's First Law, baby: An object in motion WILL STAY IN MOTION.<br /><br />+ Society. Why does every future society just decide religion is stupid? Wouldn't a NEW religion have evolved--such as one idolizing the stars? Why are the only new words "floppies" and "chutz"? Why is "chutz" used for EVERYTHING from "being brave" to a d-ag?<br /><br />+ Sketchy Transitions. Sometimes people will just start to move or leave a place with little to no warning. For instance, Eldest says "come", then suddenly, Elder is jogging to catch up with the apparently moving Eldest.<br /><br />+ Viewpoints. I can't tell you how many times I had to go to the beginning of the chapter to see who was narrating! It seemed to be worse the further in the book I got.<br /><br />+ Stereotypical characters. Eldest likes Hilter; therefore, he is a bad guy. Orion has long hair and acts crazy; therefore, he is crazy. Doc is a doctor; therefore, he is a neat freak. Harley paints; therefore, he is a tortured genius. We need to bump off Jason, make sure no one misses him (particularly Amy), so let's make him a two-timer.<br /><br />+Technology. Even with the reasons in the book, it is weird how little has changed. There are wi-coms, but why not create them to be activated mentally instead of by touching your hand to your ear? Why not have them also be listening devices? Floppies seem strange--paper-thin computers? (And I literally mean paper-thin) Why not just wire it through the wi-com? Grav tubes, wi-coms, and floppies are the only new inventions in the ~250 years of traveling? By that same logic, in 2011, we should still be using plows and horse drawn carriages.<br /><br />So...while I really liked the book, I really had some problems with the world-building, as you can see. This is a clever book, with an interesting story and good ideas, but I don't think it pushes far enough. I don't expect Arthur C. Clarke hard scifi, but a little more facts mixed in would have been nice in addition to some serious editting in the middle section. Even with the flaws, I defintiely will be checking out the sequel.<br /><br />ETA: Five years after this review, I find myself with zero desire to return to this world. I've grown up and out of young adult; if I found it cheesy and flawed back when I read this, reading the sequels would end up being the opposite of pleasurable. So although I bought the other two books, I will be selling them/donating unread.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16830249375582077601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('S1U2BdNPwjDQH8os/txJT8rnOhrC0PRGvWm/EuVWI3Zxc1/XaBELWHc0fk0JKUOQHLjd0gxdeiHmF/mjKBXR7A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yGAQo24oZbnJW/b2pHW0SfQ9sKoVraKh5fjSh4ga1PfyRnlx1Xas0W5wQpdTgL6WImJXYtsgLMa+hpQ2RVkmbQ==')})
  }
